  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1c45e10f-3142-4e5d-ab2d-cf34e62dd558'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="review_201830081" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201830081" />
    <a title="Lora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4632071-lora"><img alt="Lora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305237530p2/4632071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201830081?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lora" href="/user/show/4632071-lora">Lora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201830081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14584051285712427069">Curran's POV Vol 1 is a free, online collection of four short scenes from Curran's POV set in the Kate Daniels series. There is one scene for each of the first four books in the series.<br/><br/>The first scene is when Curran and Kate first meet. It was definitely interesting to read his initial thoughts about Kate. And if you thought the <i>"Here, kitty, kitty, kitty"</i> thing was funny in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38619.Magic_Bites__Kate_Daniels___1_' title='Magic Bites (Kate Daniels, #1) by Ilona Andrews' rel='nofollow noopener'>Magic Bites</a>, just wait until you read Curran's reaction to it. That had me rolling.<br/><br/>The second is when Kate is injured and </span>
  <span id="freeText14584051285712427069" style="display:none">Curran's POV Vol 1 is a free, online collection of four short scenes from Curran's POV set in the Kate Daniels series. There is one scene for each of the first four books in the series.<br /><br />The first scene is when Curran and Kate first meet. It was definitely interesting to read his initial thoughts about Kate. And if you thought the <i>"Here, kitty, kitty, kitty"</i> thing was funny in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38619.Magic_Bites__Kate_Daniels___1_" title="Magic Bites (Kate Daniels, #1) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Bites</a>, just wait until you read Curran's reaction to it. That had me rolling.<br /><br />The second is when Kate is injured and Curran is unsure of whether Doolittle can save her. I think this is when Curran first begins to realize that he feels more than just irritation toward Kate. It was sweet to see the moment when he began to really care for her.<br /><br />The third short scene is the one where Curran is trapped in the cage and must convince Julie to let him out. <s>Personally, out of all of the possible scenes from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4345498.Magic_Strikes__Kate_Daniels___3_" title="Magic Strikes (Kate Daniels, #3) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Strikes</a>, I would've prefered the hot tub scene, but that's just me.</s> All jokes aside, this scene was funny, cute, and insightful. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I had no idea that there was something brewing between Jim and Dali until Curran mentioned it in this scene. Goes to show you how perceptive I am! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br /><i>"She had broken into my place, messed up my weights, and even put catnip into my bed. In retaliation I had glued that cute butt of hers into her office chair. In short we were doing the mating dance."</i><br /><br />That quote is taken from the fourth, and my personal favorite, scene.<br /><br />If there's one thing that I've learned from reading this it is that Curran's POV is often as humorous as Kate's, and reading this has reaffirmed my love for the Beast Lord.<br /><br />You can read this collection <a href="http://www.smashwords.com/books/view/18799" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> for free.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14584051285712427069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1629998151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1629998151" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1629998151?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9487274-curran-vol-i">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-kindle">books-i-own-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=review-coming-soon">review-coming-soon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1629998151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18142620116340893131"><b>1st Read - September 2013</b><br/><b>2nd Read - June 2016</b><br/><br/><b>1st Read</b><br/><br/>I LOVE Curran so I was excited to get inside his head and see some of the pivotal scenes from the series from his POV. This free ebook contains scenes from each of the first four books in the series (Magic Bites, Magic Burns, Magic Strikes & Magic Bleeds) and I would recommend reading each one after the book in question.<br/><br/>I always wanted to know what went through Curran's head when he first met Kate (remember the "Here kitty, kitty, kitty" line?</span>
  <span id="freeText18142620116340893131" style="display:none"><b>1st Read - September 2013</b><br /><b>2nd Read - June 2016</b><br /><br /><b>1st Read</b><br /><br />I LOVE Curran so I was excited to get inside his head and see some of the pivotal scenes from the series from his POV. This free ebook contains scenes from each of the first four books in the series (Magic Bites, Magic Burns, Magic Strikes &amp; Magic Bleeds) and I would recommend reading each one after the book in question.<br /><br />I always wanted to know what went through Curran's head when he first met Kate (remember the "Here kitty, kitty, kitty" line?) and it was just as funny as I thought it would be! It was so good to see how Curran's opinion of Kate changed as he got to know her and my only complaint is that I wanted more.<br /><br />Kate Daniels fans are going to love these little extras but I'll warn you now this isn't a good place to start if you're unfamiliar with the series. They aren't full length stories so taken out of context they'll mean very little but for those of us who've read and loved the books they are perfect.<br /><br />______________________<br /><br /><b>2nd Read</b><br /><br />This volume contains quite a few different Curran POV's that slot in around the first 4 books in the Kate Daniels series:<br /><br />Magic Bites POV:<br />Unicorn Lane - see Kate and Curran's first meeting through his eyes<br /><br />Magic Burns POV:<br />Soup - Curran's side of the story when he offers food to an injured Kate<br /><br />Magic Strikes POV:<br />Midnight Games - Curran's reaction when he finds out exactly what Kate and the others are up to<br /><br />Magic Bleeds POV:<br />Conclave - What Curran thought when he arrived at Conclave and found Kate all dressed up and apparently on a date with Saiman<br /><br />I loved these shorts, the Midnight Games short one didn't quite tie in with the way things happened in the main book (you can tell they weren't written at the same time anyway!) but I will never get to spend enough time in Curran's head so I will happily devour any of these shorts that I can get my hands on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18142620116340893131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="valee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="valee" href="/user/show/2320890-valee">valee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer148989402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7676785892081405738">3.5 STARS<br/><br/>While I enjoyed reading things from Curran's POV, I don't thing it changed anything. We could see how he felt in all the books clearly even though things were from Kate's POV. The author had a way of letting us know how Curran felt. So I felt I didn't really need this book. But it was nice at the same time. I enjoyed it because it was short, but it felt like reading the same things over again.<br/><br/>I love Curran but this book helped me realize that it is because of Kate that I love this serie</span>
  <span id="freeText7676785892081405738" style="display:none">3.5 STARS<br /><br />While I enjoyed reading things from Curran's POV, I don't thing it changed anything. We could see how he felt in all the books clearly even though things were from Kate's POV. The author had a way of letting us know how Curran felt. So I felt I didn't really need this book. But it was nice at the same time. I enjoyed it because it was short, but it felt like reading the same things over again.<br /><br />I love Curran but this book helped me realize that it is because of Kate that I love this series so much. She is funny, brave and an ass-kicker! The best type pf heroine. She is the soul of this series and I like her POV the best. Maybe I would have enjoyed the scenes from Curran's POV better if they had been scenes we could have not appreciated from Kate's POV. But all the scenes in this book had developed in the previous books, so it felt a bit repetitive. <br /><br />What I liked the most about this book was that we got to see the scene where he met Kate, another where he started to like her, and another where he realized he wanted all from her. I like that this author makes it seem like an evolving relationship. He may not have believed she was the sexiest women in the world but there was something he liked about her, and then that something just became stronger.<br /><br />Nice read but you own't be loosing a thing for not reading it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7676785892081405738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14670257760325452558">When I first saw this, I was excited to get a glimpse of what Curran was thinking during key moments with Kate. I know this wasn't written by Ilona, so I didn't expect her writing style. I also knew they would more like snippets of a plot instead of the full story. However, I did expect good writing, and unfortunately, this didn't deliver. I get that it's a free story, but would it be too much to expect that it would be proof read? There were typographical errors galore. In addition, and this ma</span>
  <span id="freeText14670257760325452558" style="display:none">When I first saw this, I was excited to get a glimpse of what Curran was thinking during key moments with Kate. I know this wasn't written by Ilona, so I didn't expect her writing style. I also knew they would more like snippets of a plot instead of the full story. However, I did expect good writing, and unfortunately, this didn't deliver. I get that it's a free story, but would it be too much to expect that it would be proof read? There were typographical errors galore. In addition, and this may just be my complaint, this didn't quite sound like Curran. The writing didn't flow or feel natural. It was stiff and formal in a way Curran never is. I hate to say it, but this reminded me more of badly written fanfiction than an actual published story. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14251973087459819944"><b> 4 1/2 to 5 stars</b><br/><br/>Excerpt from <i>Unicorn Lane</i><br/>(Scene from "Magic Bites")<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[

  <b> <i>Moonlight from gaps in the ceiling illuminated the scene as she stepped through the gap. She came in sideways, slowly and carefully, carrying a sword. An odd-looking blade, pale. She held it like she knew what she was doing, but her faith in its ability to protect her was misplaced. The tips of my claws, wanting to come out, caused the inside of my skin to itch.   <span id="freeText14251973087459819944" style="display:none"><b> 4 1/2 to 5 stars</b><br /><br />Excerpt from <i>Unicorn Lane</i><br />(Scene from "Magic Bites")<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br />
  <br />
  <b> <i>Moonlight from gaps in the ceiling illuminated the scene as she stepped through the gap. She came in sideways, slowly and carefully, carrying a sword. An odd-looking blade, pale. She held it like she knew what she was doing, but her faith in its ability to protect her was misplaced. The tips of my claws, wanting to come out, caused the inside of my skin to itch. She had one sword, but I had ten claws.<br /><br />She scanned the area, stopped to listen, then moved forward again--stealthily, like a dancer--hiding in the nearest shadow before I caught a glimpse of her face. The draft brought another whiff of her scent. She paused and I knew she was peering into the gloom, trying to find me. I liked the way she moved, balanced and light, neither tiptoeing nor stiff. Nice body. Come to me, mouse, don't be scared.<br /><br />She took a step forward and I saw her in profile. Exotic, strong features. Not pretty, but I liked what I saw.<br /><br />I drew my fingers through the dirt, scraping the floor a little.<br /><br />She pivoted on one foot, turning her sword. Fast. Her head snapped toward me. Dark eyes stared straight at me. I detected no fear. Instead, it was a look of challenge. So not a mouse after all, but something more. This could be interesting. I'd let her dance in the dirt a bit more. She was fun to watch.<br /><br />She crouched with her hand out. What the hell was she doing...?<br /><br />"Here, kitty, kitty, kitty." </i> </b>
  <br />
  <br />
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />***<br /><br />Very cool that there are extra scenes from Curran's POV. <br /><br />Of course, I can't (or should I say won't?) read them all since I've only read the first book in this series at this point in time, but the extra tidbits for "Magic Bites" (<i>Unicorn Lane</i> and <i>Fernando's</i>) were a wee tasty treat. <br /><br />I'll be back for more...<br /><br />***<br /><br />For those of you who might be interested:<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/60750-curran-pov" rel="nofollow noopener">Curran POV Series Info on Goodreads</a><br /><br /><a href="http://www.ilona-andrews.com/curran-pov-collection/" rel="nofollow noopener">Curran POV Collection (Free download)</a></span>

<div id="review_513550017" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/513550017" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365166675p2/13954899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513550017?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=quickreads">quickreads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=fantastical-romance">fantastical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513550017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13395156960245218756">I want to say 3 stars, but I just don't see it.<i> Curran </i> goes with the Kate Daniel's series, written primarily by Ilona Andrews. Her husband Gordon wrote this. I first read the series through book 5, then I bought this little piece, to avoid spoiling the stories. However, it is fine to read it after book 4, since it has a scene, told from Curran's POV, from events that took place in books 1-4 (or skip it -- it adds nothing to the series, plot wise). <br/><br/>About 33 pages in length, and self-published, i</span>
  <span id="freeText13395156960245218756" style="display:none">I want to say 3 stars, but I just don't see it.<i> Curran </i> goes with the Kate Daniel's series, written primarily by Ilona Andrews. Her husband Gordon wrote this. I first read the series through book 5, then I bought this little piece, to avoid spoiling the stories. However, it is fine to read it after book 4, since it has a scene, told from Curran's POV, from events that took place in books 1-4 (or skip it -- it adds nothing to the series, plot wise). <br /><br />About 33 pages in length, and self-published, it only cost .99 cents on Amazon, but originally it was free, intended as a gift to faithful fans. Sadly, it is littered with typos. I was surprised that such accomplished authors would release such sloppy work.<br /><br />The series is written in Kate's POV, so a goal of this book is to show Curran's POV, especially his thoughts about Kate. A good goal, but Curran's inner dialogue was disappointing, IMO. I guess I expected the Beast Lord's thoughts to reflect keen intelligence and shrewd perception, as well as some loneliness, need, drive, integrity, and fire. I had hoped Curran's thoughts would be akin to the intelligent yet emotionally charged ruminations of William the changeling wolf, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7130616.Bayou_Moon__The_Edge___2_" title="Bayou Moon (The Edge, #2) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Bayou Moon</a>. One reason I liked<i> Bayou Moon</i> is because the authors made William so authentic, tugging on my heartstrings through his POV, which clearly revealed his brilliant mind, his need to protect and avenge the children, his never-ending loneliness, and his intense desire to mate with Cerise. <br /><br />Scenes: The scene from book 3 where Curran gets info from Julie? That was pretty much a wash for me. I would have preferred to hear the lion-shifter's thoughts and feelings when he was desperately searching for Kate, who was in such dire straights at the end of book 3. <br /><br />But some scenes are fun. I liked the scene outside Unicorn Lane best, where Kate calls out, "Here, kitty, kitty, kitty!" to Curran. Haha! And I liked the soup scene, when Curran fed Kate. Again, amusing.<br /><br />Tentatively recommended to diehard fans who can't get enough of Curran.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13395156960245218756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15999589627789450457">Although I love, love, love Curran, I don't think I liked being inside his head. It was funny and pretty awesome seeing his POV for some of my favorite scenes in Kate's books. I guess I got used to Kate's thoughts and not so much Curran and his very short thoughts.<br/><br/>Curran makes me smile every time he appears in a scene! I loved hearing his reasoning for the soup. You know, I was wondering why he held the bowl and looked at it for a while! That part made me smile all over again. <br/><br/>One of my favorite</span>
  <span id="freeText15999589627789450457" style="display:none">Although I love, love, love Curran, I don't think I liked being inside his head. It was funny and pretty awesome seeing his POV for some of my favorite scenes in Kate's books. I guess I got used to Kate's thoughts and not so much Curran and his very short thoughts.<br /><br />Curran makes me smile every time he appears in a scene! I loved hearing his reasoning for the soup. You know, I was wondering why he held the bowl and looked at it for a while! That part made me smile all over again. <br /><br />One of my favorite parts is when he sees Kate after she was attacked by these freaky looking mermaid lady things and almost dies. She was rescued by Curran and had recently woken up. She is described as having dark, puffy circles under her eyes, and her face looked gaunt.<br /><br />So anyway, Curran sees her and says (Oh! I edited just like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/82781.The_Murder_Of_Bindy_Mackenzie" rel="nofollow noopener">Bindy</a> would):<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I was not used to seeing her like this. I scared me a little bit.<br /><br />"You look like SCOUT." Honesty is important in any relationship.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Hahahahaha!<br /><br />Even though I didn't really like this, I still love Curran and would have likely kept reading even if this went up to 500 pages. That being said, only read this if you've already read the first 3 books at least. Otherwise you'll be spoiled!<br /></span>

Here you go.<br/><br/><b>Soup</b><br/><br/>And who could forget the notorious feeding of soup? NOT ME. Maybe my favorite of the POVs.<br/><br/><b>Midnight Games</b><br/><br/>This one cove</span>

Not only is it fantastic to know what Curran is thinking when he tricks Kate into accepting his suit, but you get to see his distress over the state of her health that put her in a position to be fed soup in the first place. Maybe my favorite of the POVs.<br /><br /><b>Midnight Games</b><br /><br />This one covers everything that happened from the time that Kate tricked Curran into the loup cage and Julie letting him out. Curran calls Julie something that is ridiculously cute, but I'm not going to ruin it for you by telling you what it is. <br /><br /><b>Conclave</b><br /><br />This is what went on in Curran's head when he showed up for the Pack/People/etc. meeting at Bernard's, and saw Kate there with Saiman. HIGHLY entertaining.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1822096343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10466807881647912396">I loved this collection of scenes in Curran's POV. I've read all of the books that are currently out in the Kate Daniels series, and I have to say that I love all the books. Kate is a strong, badass heroine that doesn't take shit from anyone. It is interesting to read scenes in Curran's POV instead of Kate's, and it brings a level of complexity to a story line that you already love. I look forward to more scenes in Curran's POV. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nP7cDGs1mUBZ6305QbuVhcHXHJCxs0q/CZ4ObPwEfVyer+Lb1dMGX+ae9ryJAmfW/VG/kbPiVau4NNWx0eHqrw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3GGc6AVCubneEGVBGz7KlofXCh5l3tDEMLiayEE6n/3eMKI/u6QmpmFl7sTThzjFu1GpH2ePz9CBEkEVbN8IDg==')})
  }
